They are the product of two functions, one that depends on latitude and one on longitude. The function of longitude is zero along zero or more great circles passing through the North and South Poles; the number of such <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nodal_line" title="Nodal line">nodal lines</a></i> is the absolute value of the <i>order</i> <span class="texhtml"><var>m</var></span>. The function of latitude is zero along zero or more latitude circles; this plus the order is equal to the <i>degree</i> &#8467;. Each harmonic is equivalent to a particular arrangement of magnetic charges at the center of the Earth. A <i><a href="/wiki/Magnetic_monopole" title="Magnetic monopole">monopole</a></i> is an isolated magnetic charge, which has never been observed. A <i><a href="/wiki/Magnetic_dipole" title="Magnetic dipole">dipole</a></i> is equivalent to two opposing charges brought close together and a <i><a href="/wiki/Quadrupole" title="Quadrupole">quadrupole</a></i> to two dipoles brought together. A quadrupole field is shown in the lower figure on the right.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMMch2_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-MMMch2-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Spherical harmonics can represent any <a href="/wiki/Scalar_field" title="Scalar field">scalar field</a> (function of position) that satisfies certain properties. A magnetic field is a <a href="/wiki/Vector_field" title="Vector field">vector field</a>, but if it is expressed in Cartesian components <span class="texhtml"><var>X, Y, Z</var></span>, each component is the derivative of the same scalar function called the <i><a href="/wiki/Magnetic_potential" title="Magnetic potential">magnetic potential</a></i>. Analyses of the Earth\'s magnetic field use a modified version of the usual spherical harmonics that differ by a multiplicative factor. A least-squares fit to the magnetic field measurements gives the Earth\'s field as the sum of spherical harmonics, each multiplied by the best-fitting  <i>Gauss coefficient</i> <span class="texhtml"><var>g<sub>m</sub></var><sup>&#8467;</sup></span> or <span class="texhtml"><var>h<sub>m</sub></var><sup>&#8467;</sup></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMMch2_12-6"><a href="#cite_note-MMMch2-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lowest-degree Gauss coefficient, <span class="texhtml"><var>g</var><sub>0</sub><sup>0</sup></span>, gives the contribution of an isolated magnetic charge, so it is zero. The next three coefficients &#8211; <span class="texhtml"><var>g</var><sub>1</sub><sup>0</sup></span>, <span class="texhtml"><var>g</var><sub>1</sub><sup>1</sup></span>, and <span class="texhtml"><var>h</var><sub>1</sub><sup>1</sup></span> &#8211; determine the direction and magnitude of the dipole contribution. The best fitting dipole is tilted at an angle of about 10&#176; with respect to the rotational axis, as described earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMMch2_12-7"><a href="#cite_note-MMMch2-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Radial_dependence">Radial dependence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Earth%27s_magnetic_field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Radial dependence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Spherical harmonic analysis can be used to distinguish internal from external sources if measurements are available at more than one height (for example, ground observatories and satellites). In that case, each term with coefficient <span class="texhtml"><var>g<sub>m</sub></var><sup>&#8467;</sup></span> or <span class="texhtml"><var>h<sub>m</sub></var><sup>&#8467;</sup></span> can be split into two terms: one that decreases with radius as <span class="texhtml">1/<var>r</var><sup>&#8467;+1</sup></span> and one that <i>increases</i> with radius as <span class="texhtml"><var>r</var><sup>&#8467;</sup></span>. The increasing terms fit the external sources (currents in the ionosphere and magnetosphere). However, averaged over a few years the external contributions average to zero.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMMch2_12-8"><a href="#cite_note-MMMch2-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The remaining terms predict that the potential of a dipole source (<span class="texhtml">&#8467;=1</span>) drops off as <span class="texhtml">1/<var>r</var><sup>2</sup></span>. The magnetic field, being a derivative of the potential, drops off as <span class="texhtml">1/<var>r</var><sup>3</sup></span>. Quadrupole terms drop off as <span class="texhtml">1/<var>r</var><sup>4</sup></span>, and higher order terms drop off increasingly rapidly with the radius. The radius of the outer core is about half of the radius of the Earth. If the field at the core-mantle boundary is fit to spherical harmonics, the dipole part is smaller by a factor of about 8 at the surface, the quadrupole part by a factor of 16, and so on. Thus, only the components with large wavelengths can be noticeable at the surface. From a variety of arguments, it is usually assumed that only terms up to degree <span class="texhtml">14</span> or less have their origin in the core. These have wavelengths of about 2,000 kilometres (1,200&#160;mi) or less. Smaller features are attributed to crustal anomalies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMMch2_12-9"><a href="#cite_note-MMMch2-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_models">Global models</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Earth%27s_magnetic_field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Global models">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Geomagnetism_and_Aeronomy" title="International Association of Geomagnetism and Aeronomy">International Association of Geomagnetism and Aeronomy</a> maintains a standard global field model called the <a href="/wiki/International_Geomagnetic_Reference_Field" title="International Geomagnetic Reference Field">International Geomagnetic Reference Field</a>. It is updated every five years. The 11th-generation model, IGRF11, was developed using data from satellites (<a href="/wiki/%C3%98rsted_(satellite)" title="&#216;rsted (satellite)">&#216;rsted</a>, <a href="/wiki/CHAMP_(satellite)" title="CHAMP (satellite)">CHAMP</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SAC-C&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SAC-C (page does not exist)">SAC-C</a>) and a world network of geomagnetic observatories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The spherical harmonic expansion was truncated at degree 10, with 120 coefficients, until 2000. Subsequent models are truncated at degree 13 (195 coefficients).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another global field model, called the <a href="/wiki/World_Magnetic_Model" title="World Magnetic Model">World Magnetic Model</a>, is produced jointly by the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Centers_for_Environmental_Information" title="National Centers for Environmental Information">National Centers for Environmental Information</a> (formerly the National Geophysical Data Center) and the <a href="/wiki/British_Geological_Survey" title="British Geological Survey">British Geological Survey</a>. This model truncates at degree 12 (168 coefficients) with an approximate spatial resolution of 3,000 kilometers. It is the model used by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)</a>, the United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">Federal Aviation Administration</a> (FAA), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO), and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=International_Hydrographic_Office&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="International Hydrographic Office (page does not exist)">International Hydrographic Office</a> as well as in many civilian navigation systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A third model, produced by the <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a> (<a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GSFC" title="GSFC">GSFC</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Space_Research_Institute" title="Danish Space Research Institute">Danish Space Research Institute</a>, uses a "comprehensive modeling" approach that attempts to reconcile data with greatly varying temporal and spatial resolution from ground and satellite sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p>For users with higher accuracy needs, the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Centers_for_Environmental_Information" title="National Centers for Environmental Information">National Centers for Environmental Information</a> developed  the Enhanced Magnetic Model (EMM), which extends to degree and order 790 and resolves magnetic anomalies down to a wavelength of 56 kilometers. It was compiled from satellite, marine, aeromagnetic and ground magnetic surveys. As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Earth%27s_magnetic_field&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the latest version, EMM2017, includes data from The European Space Agency\'s Swarm satellite mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomagnetism">Biomagnetism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Earth%27s_magnetic_field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Biomagnetism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Magnetoreception" title="Magnetoreception">Magnetoreception</a></div>\n<p>Animals including birds and turtles can detect the Earth\'s magnetic field, and use the field to navigate during <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">migration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Some researchers have found that cows and wild deer tend to align their bodies north-south while relaxing, but not when the animals are under high-voltage power lines, suggesting that magnetism is responsible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burda2009_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burda2009-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_summary_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_summary-75">[75]</a></sup> Other researchers reported in 2011 that they could not replicate those findings using different <a href="/wiki/Google_Earth" title="Google Earth">Google Earth</a> images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Researchers found out that very weak electromagnetic fields disrupt the magnetic compass used by European robins and other songbirds to navigate using the Earth\'s magnetic field. Neither power lines nor cellphone signals are to blame for the electromagnetic field effect on the birds;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> instead, the culprits have frequencies between 2&#160;kHz and 5&#160;MHz. These include AM radio signals and ordinary electronic equipment that might be found in businesses or private homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Earth%27s_magnetic_field&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div
